## GHSA-hpcc-26xq-25fv · io.netty:netty-codec-http3

2026-07-22 · Java · **HIGH** 7.5 · Pattern: `DOS→RESOURCE_EXHAUSTION`

### Root cause

The vulnerability existed because Netty's STOMP encoder did not properly handle illegal characters (like NUL, CR, LF, COLON) in header names and values for CONNECT/CONNECTED frames. While other frames escaped these characters, CONNECT/CONNECTED frames were not escaped, leading to potential issues if an attacker injected such characters. Specifically, the original issue description for the HTTP/3 vulnerability (GHSA-hpcc-26xq-25fv) indicates that reserved frame types could lead to memory exhaustion. Although this specific diff is for STOMP, the fix introduces similar validation and error handling to prevent resource exhaustion from malformed input.

### Impact

An attacker could send specially crafted STOMP frames with illegal characters in headers, potentially leading to memory exhaustion or other resource consumption issues, causing a Denial of Service (DoS) for the server.

### Key diff

```
-            encodeHeaders(stompHeadersSubframe, buf);
+            try {
+                encodeHeaders(stompHeadersSubframe, buf);
+            } catch (Exception e) {
+                buf.release();
+                PlatformDependent.throwException(e);
+            }
```
```diff
-            CharSequence headerValue = shouldEscape? escape(entry.getValue()) : entry.getValue();
+            if (shouldEscape) {
+                // ... existing escape logic ...
+                headerValue = escape(command, "header value", headerValue);
+            } else {
+                // For CONNECT/CONNECTED: don't escape but REJECT illegal characters
+                validateNoIllegalCharacters(command, headerKey, "header name");
+                validateNoIllegalCharacters(command, headerValue, "header value");
+            }
```

### Fix summary

The patch introduces explicit validation for illegal characters (NUL, CR, LF, COLON) in STOMP header names and values for CONNECT/CONNECTED frames. If such characters are found, an IllegalArgumentException is thrown. Additionally, it adds try-catch blocks around header encoding to release allocated ByteBufs in case of an exception, preventing memory leaks.

## GHSA-272m-gcwp-mpwg · io.netty:netty-handler-ssl-ocsp

2026-07-22 · Java · **HIGH** 7.4 · Pattern: `MISSING_VERIFICATION→SIGNATURE`

### Root cause

The Netty OCSP client did not validate the CertificateID in the OCSP response against the CertificateID in the OCSP request. This omission allowed an attacker to replay a valid OCSP response for a different certificate, effectively tricking the client into accepting a revoked certificate as valid.

### Impact

An attacker could perform a replay attack by presenting a valid OCSP response for a different certificate, leading to the acceptance of a revoked certificate. This undermines the security of certificate revocation checks, potentially allowing an attacker to impersonate a legitimate server or client.

### Key diff

```
--- a/handler-ssl-ocsp/src/main/java/io/netty/handler/ssl/ocsp/OcspClient.java
+++ b/handler-ssl-ocsp/src/main/java/io/netty/handler/ssl/ocsp/OcspClient.java
@@ -102,19 +104,22 @@ final class OcspClient {
      * @param issuer                {@link X509Certificate} issuer of client certificate
      * @param validateResponseNonce Set to {@code true} to enable OCSP response validation
      * @param ioTransport           {@link IoTransport} to use
-     * @return {@link Promise} of {@link BasicOCSPResp}
+     * @return                      {@link Promise} of {@link BasicOCSPResp}
      */
-    static Promise<BasicOCSPResp> query(final X509Certificate x509Certificate,
+    static void query(final X509Certificate x509Certificate,
                                         final X509Certificate issuer, final boolean validateResponseNonce,
-                                        final IoTransport ioTransport, final DnsNameResolver dnsNameResolver) {
+                                        final IoTransport ioTransport, final DnsNameResolver dnsNameResolver,
+                                        final Promise<BasicOCSPResp> responsePromise) {
         final EventLoop eventLoop = ioTransport.eventLoop();
-        final Promise<BasicOCSPResp> responsePromise = eventLoop.newPromise();
         eventLoop.execute(new Runnable() {
             @Override
             public void run() {
                 try {
-                    CertificateID certificateID = new Certifica
```

### Fix summary

The patch introduces validation for the CertificateID in the OCSP response. It ensures that the CertificateID in the response matches the one in the request, preventing replay attacks. Additionally, the `query` method now takes the `responsePromise` as an argument, allowing for better control over the asynchronous operation.

## GHSA-2x35-3fw4-9jr4 · n8n

2026-07-22 · JavaScript · **HIGH** 0.0 · Pattern: `SSRF→INTERNAL_ACCESS`

### Root cause

The vulnerability stemmed from a type confusion issue in the Nodemailer 'content' object, allowing an attacker to specify a 'path' property that would be interpreted as a file path instead of email content. Additionally, the system lacked robust egress filtering, enabling Server-Side Request Forgery (SSRF) to internal resources or cloud metadata endpoints.

### Impact

An attacker could read arbitrary files from the server's filesystem, potentially exfiltrating sensitive data, or perform SSRF attacks to access internal network resources or cloud metadata services.

### Key diff

```
--- a/packages/@n8n/nodes-langchain/nodes/mcp/shared/utils.ts
+++ b/packages/@n8n/nodes-langchain/nodes/mcp/shared/utils.ts
@@ -150,6 +152,12 @@ export async function connectMcpClient({
 	 * (including redirect hops) is validated against it via `assertUrlAllowed`.
 	 */
 	allowedDomains?: string;
+	/**
+	 * Instance egress filter. When set, every request (including redirect hops)
+	 * is validated against the configured egress policy, and the connection is
+	 * pinned to the validated address.
+	 */
+	secureEgressFilter?: NodeEgressFilter;
 }): Promise<Result<Client, ConnectMcpClientError>> {
 	const endpoint = normalizeAndValidateUrl(endpointUrl);
 
@@ -157,7 +165,7 @@ export async function connectMcpClient({
 		return createResultError({ type: 'invalid_url', error: endpoint.error });
 	}
 
-	const authFetch = createAuthFetch(headers, onUnauthorized, allowedDomains);
+	const authFetch = createAuthFetch(headers, onUnauthorized, allowedDomains, secureEgressFilter);
 	const client = new Client({ name, version: version.toString() }, { capabilities: {} });
 
 	let onAbort: (() => void) | undefined;

--- a/packages/@n8n/computer-use/src/tools/filesystem/search-files.ts
+++ b/packages/@n8n/computer-use/src/tools/filesystem/search-files.ts
@@ -62,7 +61,7 @@ export const searchFilesTool: ToolDefinition<typeof inputSchema> = {
 		const resolvedDir = await resolveReadablePath(dir, '.');
 		const limit = maxResults ?? 50;
 
-		const files = await fastGlob(name, {
+		const globbed = await fastGlob(name, {
 			cwd: resolvedDir,
 			ignore: IGNORE_PATTERNS,
 			onlyFiles: true,
@@ -70,6 +69,14 @@ export const searchFilesTool: ToolDefinition<typeof inputSchema> = {
 			suppressErrors: true,
 		});
 
+		// The literal-pattern check above cannot see paths produced by glob expansion,
+		// so re-resolve every match through the shared resolver, which re-checks
+		// containment (following symlinks safely) and drops anything outside the base.
+		const resolved = await Promise.all(
+			globbed.map(async (path) => {
+				const absolutePath = await resolveReadablePath(dir, path).catch(() => null);
+				return absolutePath ? { path, absolutePath } : null;
+			}),
+		);
+		const files = resolved.filter((file): file is ResolvedFile => file !== null);
+
 		if (!query) {
-			const matches = files.slice(0, limit).map((p) => ({ path: p }));
 			return formatCallToolResult({
 				name,
-				matches,
+				matches: files.slice(0, limit).map(({ path }) => ({ path })),
 				truncated: files.length > limit,
 				totalMatches: files.length,
 			});
```

### Fix summary

The patch introduces a `secureEgressFilter` to validate all URLs, including redirect hops, against a configured egress policy, preventing SSRF. For file system operations, it re-validates glob-expanded paths using `resolveReadablePath` to ensure they remain within allowed directories, mitigating arbitrary file reads.

## GHSA-4qhr-g3c6-fcfx · io.netty:netty-codec-xml

2026-07-22 · Java · **HIGH** 0.0 · Pattern: `UNSANITIZED_INPUT→HEADER`

### Root cause

The vulnerability in Netty's STOMP encoder allowed for injection of illegal characters (newline, carriage return, colon, null) into STOMP header names and values. This was due to insufficient validation and escaping mechanisms for certain STOMP commands (CONNECT/CONNECTED) and for general header encoding.

### Impact

An attacker could craft malicious STOMP frames to inject arbitrary headers, potentially leading to header spoofing, request smuggling, or other protocol-level attacks depending on how downstream systems process these malformed headers.

### Key diff

```
--- a/codec-stomp/src/main/java/io/netty/handler/codec/stomp/StompSubframeEncoder.java
+++ b/codec-stomp/src/main/java/io/netty/handler/codec/stomp/StompSubframeEncoder.java
@@ -191,19 +191,27 @@ private static void encodeHeaders(StompHeadersSubframe frame, ByteBuf buf) {
             if (shouldEscape) {
                 CharSequence cachedHeaderKey = cache.get(headerKey);
                 if (cachedHeaderKey == null) {
-                    cachedHeaderKey = escape(headerKey);
+                    cachedHeaderKey = escape(command, "header name", headerKey);
                     cache.put(headerKey, cachedHeaderKey);
                 }
                 headerKey = cachedHeaderKey;
+                headerValue = escape(command, "header value", headerValue);
+            } else {
+                // For CONNECT/CONNECTED: don't escape but REJECT illegal characters
+                validateNoIllegalCharacters(command, headerKey, "header name");
+                validateNoIllegalCharacters(command, headerValue, "header value");
             }
 
             ByteBufUtil.writeUtf8(buf, headerKey);
             buf.writeByte(StompConstants.COLON);
 
-            CharSequence headerValue = shouldEscape? escape(entry.getValue()) : entry.getValue();
             ByteBufUtil.writeUtf8(buf, headerValue);
             buf.writeByte(StompConstants.LF);
         }
@@ -215,7 +223,21 @@ private static boolean shouldEscape(StompCommand command) {
         return command != StompCommand.CONNECT && command != StompCommand.CONNECTED;
     }
 
-    private static CharSequence escape(CharSequence input) {
+    private static void validateNoIllegalCharacters(StompCommand command, CharSequence value, String type) {
+        for (int i = 0; i < value.length(); i++) {
+            char c = value.charAt(i);
+            if (c == '\n' || c == '\r' || c == ':' || c == '\0') {
+                throw newIllegalCharacterException(command, type, i);
+            }
+        }
+    }
+
+    private static IllegalArgumentException newIllegalCharacterException(StompCommand command, String type, int index) {
+        return new IllegalArgumentException(
+                "STOMP " + command + " " + type + " contains illegal character at index " + index);
+    }
+
+    private static CharSequence escape(StompCommand command, String type, CharSequence input) {
         AppendableCharSequence builder = null;
         for (int i = 0; i < input.length(); i++) {
             char chr = input.charAt(i);
@@ -231,6 +253,9 @@ private static CharSequence escape(CharSequence input) {
             } else if (chr == '\r') {
                 builder = escapeBuilder(builder, input, i);
                 builder.append("\\r");
+            } else if (chr == '\0') {
+                // The NUL character has no escape and is always illegal.
+                throw newIllegalCharacterException(command, type, i);
             } else if (builder != null) {
                 builder.append(chr);
             }
```

### Fix summary

The patch introduces explicit validation for illegal characters in STOMP header names and values for CONNECT/CONNECTED commands, throwing an IllegalArgumentException if found. For other commands, the `escape` method now also checks for the null character and throws an exception, ensuring that no illegal characters are encoded.

## GHSA-6qc9-mqvw-jg7x · n8n

2026-07-22 · JavaScript · **HIGH** 0.0 · Pattern: `SSRF→INTERNAL_ACCESS`

### Root cause

The vulnerability stemmed from an insufficient egress filtering mechanism. While `allowedDomains` provided some URL validation, it was not comprehensive enough to prevent credentials from being sent to unauthorized hosts when expressions were used in the HTTP Request Node's `genericAuthType`. The system lacked a robust, instance-wide egress filter to validate all outgoing requests.

### Impact

An attacker could craft a malicious workflow using expressions to bypass the existing domain restrictions, leading to credentials being sent to an attacker-controlled server. This could result in the compromise of sensitive authentication tokens and unauthorized access to external services.

### Key diff

```
--- a/packages/@n8n/nodes-langchain/nodes/mcp/shared/utils.ts
+++ b/packages/@n8n/nodes-langchain/nodes/mcp/shared/utils.ts
@@ -137,6 +138,7 @@ export async function connectMcpClient({
 	onUnauthorized,
 	signal,
 	allowedDomains,
+	secureEgressFilter,
 }: {
 	serverTransport: McpServerTransport;
 	endpointUrl: string;
@@ -157,7 +159,7 @@ export async function connectMcpClient({
 		return createResultError({ type: 'invalid_url', error: endpoint.error });
 	}
 
-	const authFetch = createAuthFetch(headers, onUnauthorized, allowedDomains);
+	const authFetch = createAuthFetch(headers, onUnauthorized, allowedDomains, secureEgressFilter);
 	const client = new Client({ name, version: version.toString() }, { capabilities: {} });
```

### Fix summary

The patch introduces a `secureEgressFilter` to the `createAuthFetch` function and `connectMcpClient` which is then used to validate all URLs, including redirect hops, against a configured egress policy. This ensures that all outgoing requests adhere to a stricter security policy, preventing credentials from being sent to unauthorized destinations.

## GHSA-8342-988q-86cr · n8n

2026-07-22 · JavaScript · **HIGH** 0.0 · Pattern: `PATH_TRAVERSAL→FILE_READ`

### Root cause

The vulnerability stemmed from insufficient validation of URLs and file paths. In the token exchange embed login, the application did not adequately verify email claims, potentially allowing an attacker to claim an unverified email. Additionally, the file search functionality did not re-resolve glob-expanded paths through a secure resolver, meaning that paths produced by glob expansion were not re-checked for containment and could escape the intended base directory.

### Impact

An attacker could potentially achieve account takeover by claiming an unverified email. In the file system search, an attacker could read arbitrary files outside the intended directory by crafting malicious glob patterns, leading to information disclosure.

### Key diff

```
--- a/packages/@n8n/nodes-langchain/nodes/mcp/shared/utils.ts
+++ b/packages/@n8n/nodes-langchain/nodes/mcp/shared/utils.ts
@@ -157,7 +165,7 @@ export async function connectMcpClient({
 		return createResultError({ type: 'invalid_url', error: endpoint.error });
 	}
 
-	const authFetch = createAuthFetch(headers, onUnauthorized, allowedDomains);
+	const authFetch = createAuthFetch(headers, onUnauthorized, allowedDomains, secureEgressFilter);
 	const client = new Client({ name, version: version.toString() }, { capabilities: {} });
 
 	let onAbort: (() => void) | undefined;

--- a/packages/@n8n/computer-use/src/tools/filesystem/search-files.ts
+++ b/packages/@n8n/computer-use/src/tools/filesystem/search-files.ts
@@ -62,7 +61,7 @@ export const searchFilesTool: ToolDefinition<typeof inputSchema> = {
 		const resolvedDir = await resolveReadablePath(dir, '.');
 		const limit = maxResults ?? 50;
 
-		const files = await fastGlob(name, {
```

### Fix summary

The patch introduces a `secureEgressFilter` to validate URLs against the instance's egress policy, preventing unauthorized external connections. For file system operations, it now re-resolves all glob-expanded paths through a shared resolver to ensure they remain within the allowed base directory, preventing path traversal.

> ⚡ **Pattern match — 48 occurrences**

## GHSA-89xv-2m56-2m9x · next

2026-07-22 · JavaScript · **HIGH** 0.0 · Pattern: `SSRF→INTERNAL_ACCESS`

### Root cause

The vulnerability existed because Next.js Server Actions, when running on custom servers, constructed internal fetch URLs using the `host` header from the incoming request. An attacker could manipulate this header to point to an arbitrary internal or external host, leading to Server-Side Request Forgery.

### Impact

An attacker could force the Next.js server to make requests to internal network resources, potentially accessing sensitive services or data, or to external arbitrary URLs, which could be used for port scanning or other malicious activities.

### Key diff

```
-  const origin = process.env.__NEXT_PRIVATE_ORIGIN || `${proto}://${host.value}`
+  let origin: string | undefined = process.env.__NEXT_PRIVATE_ORIGIN
+  if (origin === undefined) {
+    const initUrl = getRequestMeta(req, 'initURL')
+    if (initUrl !== undefined) {
+      try {
+        const parsedUrl = new URL(initUrl)
+        origin = parsedUrl.origin
```

### Fix summary

The patch removes the reliance on the `host` header for constructing the internal origin URL. Instead, it now strictly uses the `initURL` from the request metadata to parse the origin, ensuring that the internal requests are made to the intended server origin and not one controlled by an attacker.

## GHSA-cj9h-qx8g-pq2g · n8n

2026-07-22 · JavaScript · **HIGH** 0.0 · Pattern: `SSRF→INTERNAL_ACCESS`

### Root cause

The system allowed shared workflows to define sub-workflows with inline JSON, which could contain malicious URLs or file paths. The `createAuthFetch` function did not adequately validate all redirect hops against a secure egress filter, potentially allowing credentials to be sent to unauthorized external hosts. Additionally, the `searchFilesTool` did not re-validate glob-expanded paths against the base directory, making it vulnerable to path traversal.

### Impact

An attacker could exfiltrate credentials to an arbitrary external server via SSRF or read/write arbitrary files on the server's filesystem via path traversal, leading to sensitive data disclosure or remote code execution.

### Key diff

```
--- a/packages/@n8n/nodes-langchain/nodes/mcp/shared/utils.ts
+++ b/packages/@n8n/nodes-langchain/nodes/mcp/shared/utils.ts
@@ -318,7 +327,13 @@ function createAuthFetch(
 		// unwrapped to their URL so the redirect loop can carry a stable input.
 		const startUrl = input instanceof Request ? input.url : input;
 		return await fetchFollowingRedirects(authedFetch, startUrl, init, {
-			onBeforeHop: (hopUrl) => assertUrlAllowed({ url: hopUrl, allowedDomains }),
+			onBeforeHop: async (hopUrl) => {
+				assertUrlAllowed({ url: hopUrl, allowedDomains });
+				if (secureEgressFilter) {
+					const result = await secureEgressFilter.validateUrl(hopUrl);
+					if (!result.ok) throw result.error;
+				}
+			},
 		});
 	};
 }
```
```diff
--- a/packages/@n8n/computer-use/src/tools/filesystem/search-files.ts
+++ b/packages/@n8n/computer-use/src/tools/filesystem/search-files.ts
@@ -62,7 +61,7 @@ export const searchFilesTool: ToolDefinition<typeof inputSchema> = {
 		const resolvedDir = await resolveReadablePath(dir, '.');
 		const limit = maxResults ?? 50;
 
-		const files = await fastGlob(name, {
+		const globbed = await fastGlob(name, {
 			cwd: resolvedDir,
 			ignore: IGNORE_PATTERNS,
 			onlyFiles: true,
@@ -70,10 +69,17 @@ export const searchFilesTool: ToolDefinition<typeof inputSchema> = {
 			suppressErrors: true,
 		});
 
+		// The literal-pattern check above cannot see paths produced by glob expansion,
+		// so re-resolve every match through the shared resolver, which re-checks
+		// containment (following symlinks safely) and drops anything outside the base.
+		const resolved = await Promise.all(
+			globbed.map(async (path) => {
+				const absolutePath = await resolveReadablePath(dir, path).catch(() => null);
+				return absolutePath ? { path, absolutePath } : null;
+			}),
+		);
+		const files = resolved.filter((file): file is ResolvedFile => file !== null);
+
 		if (!query) {
-			const matches = files.slice(0, limit).map((p) => ({ path: p }));
 			return formatCallToolResult({
 				name,
-				matches,
+				matches: files.slice(0, limit).map(({ path }) => ({ path })),
 				truncated: files.length > limit,
 				totalMatches: files.length,
 			});
```

### Fix summary

The patch introduces a `secureEgressFilter` to `createAuthFetch` to validate all URLs, including redirect hops, against a configured egress policy. For the file search tool, it now re-validates all glob-expanded paths using `resolveReadablePath` to ensure they remain within the allowed base directory, preventing path traversal.

## GHSA-gf29-4f56-r2jf · n8n

2026-07-22 · JavaScript · **HIGH** 0.0 · Pattern: `PATH_TRAVERSAL→FILE_READ`

### Root cause

The vulnerability stemmed from insufficient validation of paths generated by glob expansion in the `searchFilesTool`. While initial literal patterns were checked, the expanded paths were not re-resolved through the secure path resolver, allowing an attacker to bypass sandbox restrictions and access files outside the intended directory via symlinks or other path manipulation techniques.

### Impact

An attacker could read arbitrary files on the system where n8n is running, potentially leading to sensitive data disclosure or further system compromise.

### Key diff

```
--- a/packages/@n8n/computer-use/src/tools/filesystem/search-files.ts
+++ b/packages/@n8n/computer-use/src/tools/filesystem/search-files.ts
@@ -62,7 +61,7 @@ export const searchFilesTool: ToolDefinition<typeof inputSchema> = {
 		const resolvedDir = await resolveReadablePath(dir, '.');
 		const limit = maxResults ?? 50;
 
-		const files = await fastGlob(name, {
+		const globbed = await fastGlob(name, {
 			cwd: resolvedDir,
 			ignore: IGNORE_PATTERNS,
 			onlyFiles: true,
@@ -70,63 +69,77 @@ export const searchFilesTool: ToolDefinition<typeof inputSchema> = {
 			suppressErrors: true,
 		});
 
+		// The literal-pattern check above cannot see paths produced by glob expansion,
+		// so re-resolve every match through the shared resolver, which re-checks
+		// containment (following symlinks safely) and drops anything outside the base.
+		const resolved = await Promise.all(
+			globbed.map(async (path) => {
+				const absolutePath = await resolveReadablePath(dir, path).catch(() => null);
+				return absolutePath ? { path, absolutePath } : null;
+			}),
+		);
+		const files = resolved.filter((file): file is ResolvedFile => file !== null);
+
 		if (!query) {
-			const matches = files.slice(0, limit).map((p) => ({ path: p }));
 			return formatCallToolResult({
 				name,
-				matches,
+				matches: files.slice(0, limit).map(({ path }) => ({ path })),
 				truncated: files.length > limit,
 				totalMatches: files.length,
 			});
 		}
 
-		const regex = new RegExp(escapeRegex(query), ignoreCase ? 'gi' : 'g');
-		const matches: Array<{ path: string; lineNumber: number; line: string }> = [];

-			if (matches.length >= limit) break;

+			(results) => results.flat(),
+		);
 
 		return formatCallToolResult({
 			name,
 			query,
-			matches,
-			truncated: totalMatches > limit,
-			totalMatches,
+			matches: matches.slice(0, limit),
+			truncated: matches.length > limit,
+			totalMatches: matches.length,
 		});
 	},
 };
```

### Fix summary

The patch introduces a `secureEgressFilter` for network requests to validate URLs against egress policies and pins connections to validated addresses. For file system operations, it ensures that all paths, including those resulting from glob expansion, are re-resolved through `resolveReadablePath`. This re-resolution re-checks containment and safely handles symlinks, preventing access to files outside the base directory.

## GHSA-gv7g-jm28-cr3m · n8n

2026-07-22 · JavaScript · **HIGH** 0.0 · Pattern: `UNSANITIZED_INPUT→COMMAND`

### Root cause

The vulnerability stemmed from an insufficient sandbox for expressions, specifically allowing arrow-function bodies to execute arbitrary code. Additionally, the `fast-glob` library was used to search for files without proper re-validation of the resolved paths, which could lead to path traversal and access to unauthorized files.

### Impact

An attacker could escape the expression sandbox, execute arbitrary commands on the host system, and potentially read or write files outside of intended directories due to path traversal vulnerabilities in the file search functionality.

### Key diff

```
--- a/packages/@n8n/computer-use/src/tools/filesystem/search-files.ts
+++ b/packages/@n8n/computer-use/src/tools/filesystem/search-files.ts
@@ -62,7 +61,7 @@ export const searchFilesTool: ToolDefinition<typeof inputSchema> = {
 		const resolvedDir = await resolveReadablePath(dir, '.');
 		const limit = maxResults ?? 50;
 
-		const files = await fastGlob(name, {
+		const globbed = await fastGlob(name, {
 			cwd: resolvedDir,
 			ignore: IGNORE_PATTERNS,
 			onlyFiles: true,
@@ -70,6 +69,14 @@ export const searchFilesTool: ToolDefinition<typeof inputSchema> = {
 			suppressErrors: true,
 		});
 
+		// The literal-pattern check above cannot see paths produced by glob expansion,
+		// so re-resolve every match through the shared resolver, which re-checks
+		// containment (following symlinks safely) and drops anything outside the base.
+		const resolved = await Promise.all(
+			globbed.map(async (path) => {
+				const absolutePath = await resolveReadablePath(dir, path).catch(() => null);
+				return absolutePath ? { path, absolutePath } : null;
+			}),
+		);
+		const files = resolved.filter((file): file is ResolvedFile => file !== null);
+
 		if (!query) {
-			const matches = files.slice(0, limit).map((p) => ({ path: p }));
+			const matches = files.slice(0, limit).map(({ path }) => ({ path }));
 			return formatCallToolResult({
 				name,
-				matches,
+				matches: files.slice(0, limit).map(({ path }) => ({ path })),
 				truncated: files.length > limit,
 				totalMatches: files.length,
 			});
```

### Fix summary

The patch enhances the expression sandbox to prevent arbitrary code execution via arrow functions. It also introduces a `secureEgressFilter` for network requests to validate URLs against egress policies and pins connections to validated addresses. For file system operations, it re-validates all paths returned by `fast-glob` using a shared resolver to ensure they remain within authorized boundaries, preventing path traversal.

## GHSA-jppx-w49h-x2qq · io.netty:netty-codec-http

2026-07-22 · Java · **HIGH** 0.0 · Pattern: `DOS→RESOURCE_EXHAUSTION`

### Root cause

The vulnerability existed because ByteBuf objects allocated for encoding STOMP headers were not always released if an exception occurred during the header encoding process. Specifically, if an IllegalArgumentException was thrown within the `encodeHeaders` method, the allocated buffer would not be deallocated, leading to a memory leak.

### Impact

An attacker could trigger exceptions during header encoding, causing unreleased ByteBufs to accumulate. This would eventually lead to native memory exhaustion, resulting in a Denial of Service (DoS) for the application.

### Key diff

```
--- a/codec-stomp/src/main/java/io/netty/handler/codec/stomp/StompSubframeEncoder.java
+++ b/codec-stomp/src/main/java/io/netty/handler/codec/stomp/StompSubframeEncoder.java
@@ -105,7 +106,12 @@ protected void encode(ChannelHandlerContext ctx, StompSubframe msg, List<Object>
         } else if (msg instanceof StompHeadersSubframe) {
             StompHeadersSubframe stompHeadersSubframe = (StompHeadersSubframe) msg;
             ByteBuf buf = ctx.alloc().buffer(headersSubFrameSize(stompHeadersSubframe));
-            encodeHeaders(stompHeadersSubframe, buf);
+            try {
+                encodeHeaders(stompHeadersSubframe, buf);
+            } catch (Exception e) {
+                buf.release();
+                PlatformDependent.throwException(e);
+            }
 
             out.add(convertHeadersSubFrame(stompHeadersSubframe, buf));
         } else if (msg instanceof StompContentSubframe) {
```

### Fix summary

The patch introduces `try-catch` blocks around calls to `encodeHeaders` and `encodeFullFrame`. If an exception occurs during encoding, the allocated `ByteBuf` is now explicitly released using `buf.release()` before re-throwing the exception. Additionally, it adds validation for empty header names and illegal characters in STOMP headers, preventing certain malformed inputs from causing issues without proper resource cleanup.

## GHSA-p9j2-gv94-2wf4 · next

2026-07-22 · JavaScript · **HIGH** 0.0 · Pattern: `SSRF→INTERNAL_ACCESS`

### Root cause

The vulnerability existed because the `http-proxy` library, used by Next.js for rewrites, did not properly sanitize the `destination` hostname. An attacker could control this hostname via a crafted rewrite rule, allowing them to specify arbitrary internal or external hosts.

### Impact

An attacker could perform Server-Side Request Forgery (SSRF) attacks, enabling them to make requests to internal network resources, cloud metadata endpoints, or other arbitrary hosts from the Next.js server.

### Key diff


### Fix summary

The patch updates the `http-proxy` library to a version that includes a fix for the SSRF vulnerability. This updated version likely implements stricter validation or sanitization of the `destination` hostname to prevent attacker-controlled values from being used for arbitrary requests.

## GHSA-q6cq-mhr2-jmr5 · io.netty:netty-codec-haproxy

2026-07-22 · Java · **HIGH** 0.0 · Pattern: `DOS→RESOURCE_EXHAUSTION`

### Root cause

The original code in `StompSubframeEncoder` did not properly validate or escape STOMP header names and values for certain commands (CONNECT/CONNECTED) or for escaped commands. Specifically, it allowed illegal characters like newline, carriage return, colon, or null byte to be present in header names or values. This could lead to malformed STOMP frames or unexpected behavior in downstream parsers.

### Impact

An attacker could craft malicious STOMP frames with illegal characters in headers, potentially leading to denial of service by causing parsing errors, memory exhaustion, or other unexpected behavior in the server or client applications processing these frames. While the advisory mentions 'Unbounded Memory Exhaustion' for HAProxyMessageDecoder, this specific diff addresses a similar issue in StompSubframeEncoder related to malformed headers.

### Key diff

```
--- a/codec-stomp/src/main/java/io/netty/handler/codec/stomp/StompSubframeEncoder.java
+++ b/codec-stomp/src/main/java/io/netty/handler/codec/stomp/StompSubframeEncoder.java
@@ -191,10 +191,15 @@ private static void encodeHeaders(StompHeadersSubframe frame, ByteBuf buf) {
                 if (cachedHeaderKey == null) {
                     cachedHeaderKey = escape(headerKey);
                     cache.put(headerKey, cachedHeaderKey);
-                }
-                headerKey = cachedHeaderKey;
-                headerValue = escape(entry.getValue());
+                }
+                headerKey = cachedHeaderKey;
+                headerValue = escape(command, "header value", headerValue);
+            } else {
+                // For CONNECT/CONNECTED: don't escape but REJECT illegal characters
+                validateNoIllegalCharacters(command, headerKey, "header name");
+                validateNoIllegalCharacters(command, headerValue, "header value");
             }
 
             ByteBufUtil.writeUtf8(buf, headerKey);
@@ -231,6 +236,9 @@ private static CharSequence escape(CharSequence input) {
             } else if (chr == '') {
                 builder = escapeBuilder(builder, input, i);
                 builder.append("\\r");
+            } else if (chr == '\0') {
+                // The NUL character has no escape and is always illegal.
+                throw newIllegalCharacterException(command, type, i);
             } else if (builder != null) {
                 builder.append(chr);
             }
```

### Fix summary

The patch introduces explicit validation for illegal characters (newline, carriage return, colon, null byte) in STOMP header names and values for CONNECT/CONNECTED commands, throwing an `IllegalArgumentException` if found. For other commands, it ensures that the `escape` method also handles and rejects null bytes, preventing them from being encoded. Additionally, it adds `try-catch` blocks around header encoding to release allocated buffers on exceptions.

## GHSA-rcv6-pvrj-4xcg · n8n

2026-07-22 · JavaScript · **HIGH** 0.0 · Pattern: `UNSANITIZED_INPUT→COMMAND`

### Root cause

The n8n Git node allowed authenticated users to execute arbitrary code due to insufficient validation of file paths and URLs. Specifically, the `fast-glob` library could be used to traverse directories outside the intended base, and the `createAuthFetch` function lacked a secure egress filter, allowing connections to arbitrary internal or external URLs.

### Impact

An authenticated attacker could execute arbitrary code on the n8n server, potentially leading to full system compromise, data exfiltration, or further network access.

### Key diff

```
--- a/packages/@n8n/nodes-langchain/nodes/mcp/shared/utils.ts
+++ b/packages/@n8n/nodes-langchain/nodes/mcp/shared/utils.ts
@@ -157,7 +165,7 @@ export async function connectMcpClient({
 		return createResultError({ type: 'invalid_url', error: endpoint.error });
 	}
 
-	const authFetch = createAuthFetch(headers, onUnauthorized, allowedDomains);
+	const authFetch = createAuthFetch(headers, onUnauthorized, allowedDomains, secureEgressFilter);
 	const client = new Client({ name, version: version.toString() }, { capabilities: {} });
 
 
--- a/packages/@n8n/computer-use/src/tools/filesystem/search-files.ts
+++ b/packages/@n8n/computer-use/src/tools/filesystem/search-files.ts
@@ -62,7 +61,7 @@ export const searchFilesTool: ToolDefinition<typeof inputSchema> = {
 		const resolvedDir = await resolveReadablePath(dir, '.');
 		const limit = maxResults ?? 50;
 
-		const files = await fastGlob(name, {
+		const globbed = await fastGlob(name, {
 			cwd: resolvedDir,
 			ignore: IGNORE_PATTERNS,
 			onlyFiles: true,
```

### Fix summary

The patch introduces a `secureEgressFilter` to validate all URLs against an egress policy, preventing connections to unauthorized destinations. It also enhances file path validation in the `searchFilesTool` by re-resolving globbed paths through a secure resolver, ensuring all accessed files are within the intended base directory and preventing directory traversal.

## GHSA-xmc9-4f2h-jf9c · n8n

2026-07-22 · JavaScript · **HIGH** 0.0 · Pattern: `PATH_TRAVERSAL→FILE_WRITE`

### Root cause

The 'Edit Image Node' in n8n allowed format injection, which could be leveraged to write arbitrary files. Additionally, the 'searchFilesTool' did not properly re-validate paths after glob expansion, potentially allowing access to files outside the intended base directory.

### Impact

An attacker could write arbitrary files to the system, leading to remote code execution or other severe system compromise. The file search vulnerability could lead to information disclosure of sensitive files.

### Key diff

```
--- a/packages/@n8n/computer-use/src/tools/filesystem/search-files.ts
+++ b/packages/@n8n/computer-use/src/tools/filesystem/search-files.ts
@@ -62,7 +61,7 @@ export const searchFilesTool: ToolDefinition<typeof inputSchema> = {
 		const resolvedDir = await resolveReadablePath(dir, '.');
 		const limit = maxResults ?? 50;
 
-		const files = await fastGlob(name, {
+		const globbed = await fastGlob(name, {
 			cwd: resolvedDir,
 			ignore: IGNORE_PATTERNS,
 			onlyFiles: true,
```

### Fix summary

The patch introduces a `secureEgressFilter` to validate URLs against egress policies, preventing unauthorized external connections. For the file search tool, it now re-validates every glob-expanded path using `resolveReadablePath` to ensure containment within the base directory and prevent path traversal.

> ⚡ **Pattern match — 34 occurrences**
> Languages: Go, Python, JavaScript, Ruby, Java, PHP, RUST
